## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations (ODE dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of state (x, v) and possibly time t, which is the standard form of second-order oscillator equations written as a first-order system. Nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and external/parametric forcing commonly appear as algebraic, polynomial, trigonometric, or piecewise functions of x, v, and t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (small-amplitude restoring force; sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear oscillator with viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (spring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Pendulum (exact, not small-angle): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (rotational oscillator; nonlinear restoring term)
- Softening stiffness via saturation: dv_dt = c0 * x / (c1 + x**2) + c2 * v (effective stiffness decreases with |x|)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (approximate sign(v) friction with smooth transition)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag proportional to v|v|)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (self-excited oscillator with nonlinear damping)
- Duffing–Van der Pol (combined nonlinear stiffness and damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * (c3 - x**2) * v + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (common benchmark nonlinear forced oscillator)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness; Mathieu-type behavior)
- Piecewise/contact stiffness (impact-like): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * Max(x - c3, 0) (additional stiffness after a gap/stop is engaged)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force → dv_dt depends primarily on x (often odd in x); adding only x terms suggests energy-conserving dynamics (no damping/drive).
- Viscous dissipation → a term linear in v (c*v) indicates damping proportional to velocity; sign of c determines damping vs pumping.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency → higher odd powers of x (x**3, x**5) indicate Duffing-like stiffness that shifts frequency with amplitude.
- Geometric/nonlinear spring kinematics → sin(c*x) restoring terms point to pendulum/rotational oscillators or periodically constrained motion.
- Dry friction or actuator saturation → tanh(c*v) or other bounded odd functions of v emulate sign(v) friction with smooth switching near v=0.
- Aerodynamic/hydrodynamic drag regimes → v*Abs(v) indicates quadratic drag, typically dominant at higher speeds than linear damping.
- Self-excitation/limit cycles → state-dependent damping such as (c0 - x**2)*v or v + v**3 suggests negative damping at small amplitude and positive at large amplitude.
- External periodic forcing → additive cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms imply a driven oscillator; resonance/entrainment behavior follows.
- Parametric resonance → time-multiplying stiffness (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x indicates modulation of system parameters rather than additive forcing.
- Hard impacts/stops/backlash → Max(x-c,0) or other piecewise x-dependence suggests unilateral constraints causing nonsmooth acceleration changes.

- **Candidate 6**: Has `v/(Abs(v)+1)` — this is NOT equivalent to `log(Abs(v)+1)`. These are fundamentally different functions.
